That was a big deal to me since that's the whole point of buying them in the first place. Well I tested all images and have had no issues getting any of them to transfer. I have a few tips that might help: ~ be sure to remove the plastic, blue film before doing anything else ~ images transfer much better when your base polish color is still slightly wet ~ try applying a top coat before stamping if base polish color is completely dry ~ try using a thick, opaque polish, it is NOT necessary to use konad special polish ~ be sure that you scrape ALL excess polish away with no extra goop left over the image ~ pick up the image from the plate with the rubber stamp in a rolling motion ~ look at the stamp to ensure the image transferred before applying to the nail ~ apply image to the nail in a rolling motion as the stamp and your nails are slightly rounded I hope those still skeptical will give the 17pc set a try. I'm glad I did! Good luck & happy stamping!

Hope this info helps! Helpful hints; -Make sure you remove the protective plastic cover from the front of the plates before attempting to use. -Wet a cotton ball w/ pure acetone and hold it with tweezers in order to avoid ruining the designs on your nails. Use the acetone soaked cotton ball to wipe nail polish off of the plates and stamper. The plate should be dry before applying more polish. -Use a thick highly pigmented polish for stamping. -Work fast! If you take too long the polish will dry on the plate or stamper and you will not get it to transfer. -If you are working fast and the polish does not transfer try another type of polish, some polished are extra quick drying. -Be gentle when you apply top coat or you may smear your design.

  107. I bought these plates because my daughters spent the night at a friends and came home with the cutest nails. When I asked about them their friend showed me her 'name brand' set that she paid about $50 for. It had two plates some polish, a stamper & a scraper. I thought it was adorable but was not going to pay that kind of money. Bargain hunter than I am I searched for a better deal. Which led me to Bundle Monster and another 'off brand' that I found on ebay for similar value.<br /><br />I bought both sets. The received the ebay ones first. They were a great value came with some extras & offered cute plates (a few with the same designs from one plate to the next). They even offered the same designs and our neighbor girl had on her 'name brand' plates (none of which were 'full nail' or 'french tip' images). I was quite satisfied but have to say when I received the plates from Bundle Monster I soon realized I preferred their images better. They were larger for the most part & a much nicer selection over all (I hope they continue to add to their designs).<br /><br />The ONLY Con I would mention is that the edges seem a bit sharp (compared to both the name brand & the other off brand I purchased) so I would keep them out of reach from young fingers even if they are just 'looking at the designs'. My teenage daughter cut herself on one not paying attention.<br /><br />For those of you who are having problems with them here are some tips & step by step instructions I use (mentioned by others but with so many reviews I will post it as well).<br /><br />Tips to Know Before you get started:<br /><br />1) REMOVE the plastic film: They come with a plastic film when you first receive them that sometimes can not be seen. I used something sharp (tweezers) to cut a spot & then removed the rest with my fingers. If you do not remove the film the plates do not work.<br /><br />2) Use THICK but NOT Quick Dry Contrasting Nail Polish for Images: If you do not have a 'thick' polish & do not want to spend $10+ on the 'name brand' let one of yours dry out a bit or go to your local salon that does nails & see if they have some 'old stuff' that you can buy for pennies on the dollar.<br /><br />If you use quick dry you may not get the transfer done quick enough before it drys.<br /><br />I have tried a few variations of colors but for obvious reasons white & black work best. A dark color with a white or light pink print or a light color with a black or similar dark will have the best results. Do some practice ones on something to see what you really like.<br /><br />3) Use one coat cover for Bottom Coat & Top Coat: I recommend using nail polish that IS quick dry & only takes one coat to cover for both the Bottom & Top Coats (not images). This is because the more nail polish you have on your nails the more likely it is to smear your images. Using quick dry also helps with this.<br /><br />4) Use a Good Acetone nail remover: It seems this works best for cleaning the plates. Some remover seems to thin out the polish & make it more difficult to transfer.<br /><br />5) Let the Plates DRY completely: After each transfer you will need to clean the plate (if there is polish in the image you will not get a good transfer). When you wipe the polish out let the remover dry before you put polish on it. Again it will thin out the polish making for a poor transfer.<br /><br />6) Use Cotton Rounds instead of Balls: Cotton Rounds make it a lot easier to manage the nail remover without messing up your nails. I use a nail polish remover with a pump so (one touch remover) I don't have to do too much with my hands.<br /><br />7) Between EACH STEP let your nails dry for the best possible results.<br /><br />8) If you don't have a plate holder (which I highly recommend) use double sided scotch tape to hold the plates in place on whatever you are scraping the extra paint onto.<br /><br />9) I also recommend the two sided stamper with the smaller stamp. It is much easier to ensure the best image placement for smaller images.<br /><br />10) If you have larger nail beds you may want to overlap designs. Everyone has different nail bed sizes so it would be difficult to accommodate everyone. With practice one could learn to line up the designs for a fuller image but I would recommend either using more than one design or just overlapping them. It can create a nice effect as well.<br /><br />10) Clean EVERYTHING thoroughly when you are done: This will be important so that your future painting will be more successful & so that the plates, stamper & scraper last longer.<br /><br />My personal steps:<br /><br />1) Wash hands & gently push back cuticles that might be up on nail bed.<br /><br />2) Get out all needed products & items.<br /><br />3) Paint nails with bottom coat. Let dry completely (VERY important for best results)<br /><br />4) Prepare image plate, image nail polish & cotton round with polish remover.<br /><br />5) Working Quickly - Paint a nice coat of image paint over your image, scrape away extra, stamp with stamper, line up with nail bed, roll on fast, firmly & carefully ensuring you get the entire image to transfer. (If you have never seen this done check out a youtube video on it).<br /><br />6) After each image you will have to clean the plate completely (especially if you are using the same image for each nail). Be sure to do so carefully not to smudge your other nails. Some recommend using tweezers - I find if I use a Cotton round instead of a ball I don't need to. Again let the polish remover dry on the plate before adding the polish again.<br /><br />7) I recommend doing all your images on one hand BEFORE putting on the top coat. Just be gentle not to 'bump' them.<br /><br />8) Once your first hand is complete put on your top coat & let this dry Completely before starting your second hand.<br /><br />9) Repeat for second hand!<br /><br />Once you get the hang of it use multiple designs & colors. We have used it to stamp our phones & more (and change when we get bored)<br /><br />Hope you enjoy this as much as I did! All the little Girls in my life (age appropriate of course) will be getting this for the next 'gift giving' occasion!!want to overlap designs. Everyone has different nail bed sizes so it would be difficult to accommodate everyone. With practice one could learn to line up the designs for a fuller image but I would recommend either using more than one design or just overlapping them. It can create a nice effect as well. 10) Clean EVERYTHING thoroughly when you are done: This will be important so that your future painting will be more successful & so that the plates, stamper & scraper last longer. My personal steps: 1) Wash hands & gently push back cuticles that might be up on nail bed. 2) Get out all needed products & items. 3) Paint nails with bottom coat. Let dry completely (VERY important for best results) 4) Prepare image plate, image nail polish & cotton round with polish remover. 5) Working Quickly - Paint a nice coat of image paint over your image, scrape away extra, stamp with stamper, line up with nail bed, roll on fast, firmly & carefully ensuring you get the entire image to transfer. (If you have never seen this done check out a youtube video on it). 6) After each image you will have to clean the plate completely (especially if you are using the same image for each nail). Be sure to do so carefully not to smudge your other nails. Some recommend using tweezers - I find if I use a Cotton round instead of a ball I don't need to. Again let the polish remover dry on the plate before adding the polish again. 7) I recommend doing all your images on one hand BEFORE putting on the top coat. Just be gentle not to 'bump' them. 8) Once your first hand is complete put on your top coat & let this dry Completely before starting your second hand. 9) Repeat for second hand! Once you get the hang of it use multiple designs & colors. We have used it to stamp our phones & more (and change when we get bored) Hope you enjoy this as much as I did! All the little Girls in my life (age appropriate of course) will be getting this for the next 'gift giving' occasion!!

  134. These plates are just cheaper (price-wise and quality) versions of Konad plates. You get 21 plates for about $18, and shipping is free, so that's quite an irresistible deal, but I have to say, these plates CANNOT compare to the Konad plates. First of all, there is no safety backing on the plates, as many people have written already; the plates are very thin, and can be very sharp. I resorted to pasting the plates to index cards so it's less likely to slice into my fingers, and to prevent the plates from scratching each other. Secondly, the designs of the plates are not as intricate and well done as the Konad plates. I have a bunch of Konad plates, and the BM designs definitely don't come close. The BM designs are not as detailed, and just are not as \\"pretty\\" as the Konad designs (but of course, you get what you pay for). Also, some of the plates I got, seems like there were manufacturing flaws. The designs on the plates appear smeared, or smudged, and when I tried to stamp them, the images do not transfer properly, if at all. Thridly, the full nail designs don't actually fit on your whole nail (unless you have really small hands, or are a child). I learned that if I'm very precise on how I stamp, I can get away with stamping the \\"full nail\\" designs from my index to my pinky. Thumb is definitely out of the question, lest you end up with a half stamped thumb, or you're good enough to stamp in two halves (you have to really match up the designs). I've never had this problem with Konad designs. Fourthly, some of my plates arrived with water and rust stains. I don't understand how this happens, since there is a thin Saran type film ontop the plates when you first get them. This must mean that the plates have somehow gotten wet during manufacturing process, but before the packaging process. This doens't interfere with the stamping process, but I just find it annoying to have rust and water marks on my plates. Overall, these plates are dirt cheap (under a dollarfor each plate), compared to Konad which are between $4-7 per plate, but you get what you pay for, and Bundle Monster plates definitely do NOT compare to the quality of Konad's.

  177. I got these quickly and they are great...yes they are only slightly , almost imperceivably, thinner than the Konad plates, maybe it's not so much the thickness as the type of stainess steel they use..Konad's seem to be slightly more rigid, less apt to bend or dent the plate, but both brands of plates should be cared for and used gently, it can happen to either brand. Maybe they have improved their processess but I didn't find the edges overly sharp or ragged, after all they are a thin piece of metal like the top of an aluminum can and it's true, it's possible, you could cut yourself on the plates but it's not a toy and it's more like a craft or makeup item and not intended for kids to handle carelessly. You wouldn't want a toddler getting into glue or nail polish remover type of products either.<br />As far as transferring the images goes I have only experimented a bit so far but had good luck. Just like the Konad plates there is a bit of practice and skill involved in applying the right motion and pressure to both the scraped imaged on the plate, to pick it up, and rolling it on your nail to transfer it to your nail nicely. Smearing of highly detailed images or skips in the image happens when not enough, or too much pressure is applied in both the plate and the nail stamping operations. Yes, work quickly for best results, yes, try different polishes, some work much better than others.<br />As far as using the Bundlemonster plates their aforementioned, perhaps lesser quality, stainless steel makes them slightly more flexible. I found you couldn't get a clean scrape when the plate was set on top of a mere double paper towel thickness on a table surface. The image would be smeary because you didn't get all the excess polish off the image due to a very slight flex in the plate on the slightly poofy paper towels (this would be a huge problem on a regular cloth towel) and the plate . Maybe the plate holder would help but I found holding the plate down flat with your other hand while making the scrape does the trick. Also using an old cutting board or some kind of more solid surface would keep the plate absolutely flat for the scrape. Also the metal scaper, doesn't flex at all so it doesn't follow the slight flexing of the plate when you scrape. Try using a credit card or one of those really thin plastic rewards card from a store that will flex into the image as you scrape it. These slight adjustments to use the Bundlemonster plates, even though they are a bit lesser quality than the Konad, will transfer the more detailed images without smearing.while making the scrape does the trick. Also using an old cutting board or some kind of more solid surface would keep the plate absolutely flat for the scrape. Try using a credit card or one of those really thin plastic rewards card from a store that will flex into the image as you scrape it.   453. I ordered these plates after stumbling across the concept of stamping online. I did some research and found many people stating although it's a great concept, the Konad plates are simply to overpriced. When I found the plates, and the polish, I must say I agreed. I did my research and found this bundle monster set. I am OVERJOYED with the results. There are tons of great designs. I've tried the full designs, tips, and small images, and every image I've tried so far has worked great. A few things to keep in mind, they have revised this product so they are no longer sharp. They have a protective backing so no more worries about cutting your fingers. A review on here was super helpful in teaching me how to do stamping. I did it sucesfully my first try. I'd like to help others so below is my exact experience with the plates, what else I used, and how I did it.<br /><br />1. When you recieve the plates, there is a blue plastic cover over each. Peel the covers off as you use the plates. I didn't bother removing all of them at once, I saw no reason to do so as you can see the images through the cover.<br /><br />2. I grabbed a paper plate to keep everything on. I pull out all supplies before getting started. I grabbed my polish remover pump with 100% pure acetone in it, then I grabbed the Konad stamper and scraper, q-tips, Sally Hansen Base and top coat, and 2 regular polish colors. You can choose to buy the konad stamping polish, but I did not and have been totally satisfied using OPI, Sally Hansen, and generic polish.<br /><br />3. A few tips for you. 100% pure acetone is great because it's the fastest for cleaning the plates and stamper between transfers. The pump is really useful because you can press the q-tips to the pump and get them full of remover without having to risk touching your newly painted nails to the remover. I looked at the generic stamper and found it didnt' have nearly the good reviews the konad did for only $2 more. I also read reviews that said to use a old gift card instead of the konad scraper. The gift card idea actually did not work at all for me, and the konad scraper has worked great without damaging any plates. As for polish, I'd suggest using white and black your first times stamping since they're easiest to see on the stamper. I used OPI white and Sally Hansen black. I have stamped with all OPI and sally hansen $2 polish and had no problems.<br /><br />4. Time to get started. Paint a base coat of clear polish to keep your nails from yellowing. A thin coat is best.<br /><br />5. Paint whatever color of polish you picked out to cover your whole nail (you can use these to stamp only tips, but I'd suggest doing full designs your first try) Try to pick a polish you only need one coat for, but 2 is okay. Less coats equals less change of smudging or those nasty clumps of polish that you get if your touch your still wet nail to something.<br /><br />6. Here's where the stamping comes in. You wanna be quick about it, but don't be so quick that you're sloppy. choose a polish (don't pick an instant dry polish for this, it wont work) paint a good layer of polish onto the plate. Grab your scraper and scrape it across the image to remove extra polish. Someone on here suggested taping the plate down or buying a plate holder. I've found I don't need to tape them, they don't slide on the paper plate. It also gives you one less thing to clean off. If you purchase the plate holder you'd have to get the polish off that as well. After scraping the extra polish pick up you're stamper. Use the large end for large designs and the small end for small designs. Firmly press the stamper to the plate, almost rolling it across the image to insure no smudges. The lift the stamper and look at the image on it to make sure it transfered clear. Then line the stamper up to your nail, I prefer to roll from left to right, but it's up to your preference. You don't need to press all that hard. Just roll the stamper across your nail to get the full image. After stamping you should have 1 nail completed, a side from the top coat.<br /><br />7. Take a q-tip and press it to the polish remover pump. Use the acetone remover to fully clean off your plate, scraper, and stamper. Then begin step 6 all over again and repeat until every nail is painted.<br /><br />8. After the image drys (this takes a very short ammount of time) paint a top coat to really give your nails that shine.<br /><br />9. After your top coat drys, clean up is simple if you used a paper plate. Put all of your used q-tips on the plate. All the extra polish ended up on the plate as well so no need to clean it up. Make sure your tools are all totally cleaned off. I keep my plates in a zip lock, nothing fancy. Then pick up your plate, and toss it in the trash. You're done!<br /><br />Hopefully this will be helpful to you. These plates are a really great value and I don't ever plan to buy a $5 konad plate when I got 21 plates for 17.99 and free shipping. They work wonderfuly and have tons of cute designs. I plan to purchase the 2nd set of these in the future just to get even more designs. I also read some people said that the image doesn't cover the whole finger? I'm really confused about that part. I have really long fingers, long nail beds, and long nails in general. I've had no problem getting the image to cover my whole nail. As long as you transfer the whole image it's plenty big enough. If you have wide nails simply put the image on your nail starting on one side, then stamp a half image and line it up on the right to overlap the design. I did this with my big toe since that was the only time I needed to, and it worked great. Another thing to keep in mind is you're best off having really contrasting colors. I did blue with white stamps, red with black stamps, and white with pink stamps and was really happy. I just did turqoise with silver stamps and although it's cool they blend together a little to much.

  519. I bought these last year after I had purchased the cheap tv stamper set that was being sold at Sally's. Don't buy that set if you can help it. Get a Konad stamper and pick someone else's plates.<br /><br />These Bundle plates, just like any other project/skill/product that you use have their drawbacks.<br />These plates do work well, and the newer sets come with a paper backing to protect the edges. Some people state that the images don't come through, but it really depends on a couple of things, so if your images don't come through on these plates, here are some things to keep in mind:<br />1. try a different stamper. I bought a Konad recently and it stamped beautifully, especially the delicate full-nail leaf pattern. Came out very well.<br />2. it could be your polish. Some of the wet and wild stuff works, china glaze does too, as does sally hansen. but it depends on the consistency and chemicals used in the polish, so don't be discouraged! I would recommend using the same brand of top coat that you are using to do the stamping design, because some I have used seem to \\"melt\\" the base coats away after a light brush.<br />3. it could be your technique. press firmly but evenly as you go down. Don't press hard enough to break your finger, but a little pressure may help in transfering. Also, work quickly, as the paint on the plate or stamped will dry.<br />4. it could be that you didn't clean the plate properly. I thoroughly clean out every desgin with acetone nail polish remover, and make sure all the cracks are clean. DO NOT UNDER ANY CIRCUMSTANCE USE NAIL POLISH REMOVER WITH MOISTURIZERS. THE OILS AND CHEMICALS MAY CAUSE THE NAIL POLISH NOT TO ADHERE TO THE STAMPER AND WON'T WORK!<br />5. the plate could be bad. I haven't tried every design, so I can't say which are bad, but they seemed to do okay. If you work fast and you roll the stamper in an even motion across your nails in one direction, and NOT back and forth, your design should be ok.<br />Overall, a good stamped makes a helluva lot of difference when doing this. Otherwise, they are good plates, although the rose doesn't come out too well in my opinion, and the full nail designs are too small, as many others have said. I'm not picky. I just match up and restamp the open space on the nail and it turns out good.<br />Overall, okay quality for the price and interesting designs for those who are just starting out and want to have something a little different to play with. Cheers!
